{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01MTrvfxYt5VNt1oBmUTD7Ko","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# `client-go` Architecture\n     2→\n     3→This document explains the internal architecture of `client-go` for contributors. It describes the\n     4→major components, how they interact, and the key design decisions that shape the library.\n     5→\n     6→## Client Configuration\n     7→\n     8→There is an architectural separation between loading client configuration and using it. The\n     9→`rest.Config` object is the in-memory representation of this configuration. The\n    10→`tools/clientcmd` package is the standard factory for producing it. `clientcmd` handles the\n    11→complex logic of parsing `kubeconfig` files, merging contexts, and handling external\n    12→authentication providers (e.g., OIDC).\n    13→\n    14→## REST Client\n    15→\n    16→The `rest.Client` is the foundational HTTP client that underpins all other clients. It separates\n    17→the low-level concerns of HTTP transport, serialization, and error handling from higher-level,\n    18→Kubernetes-specific object logic.\n    19→\n    20→The `rest.Config` object is used to build the underlying HTTP transport, which is typically a\n    21→chain of `http.RoundTripper` objects. Each element in the chain is responsible for a specific\n    22→task, such as adding an `Authorization` header. This is the mechanism by which all authentication\n    23→is injected into requests.\n    24→\n    25→The client uses a builder pattern for requests (e.g., `.Verb()`, `.Resource()`), deferring\n    26→response processing until a method like `.Into(&pod)` is called. This separation is key to\n    27→supporting different client models from a common base.\n    28→\n    29→### Endpoint Interactions\n    30→\n    31→*   **Content Negotiation:** The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate the wire format\n    32→    (JSON or Protobuf). A key performance optimization using this mechanism is the ability to\n    33→    request metadata-only objects via the `as=PartialObjectMetadata;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameter.\n    34→    Also the `as=Table;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameters may be used to request lists as tables. \n    35→*   **Subresources:** The client can target standard subresources like `/status` or `/scale` for\n    36→    object mutations, and it can also handle action-oriented subresources like `/logs` or\n    37→    `/exec`, which often involve streaming data.\n    38→*   **List Pagination:** For `LIST` requests, the client can specify a `limit`. The server will\n    39→    return up to that many items and, if more exist, a `continue` token. The client is\n    40→    responsible for passing this token in a subsequent request to retrieve the next page.\n    41→    Higher-level tools like the `Reflector`'s `ListerWatcher` handle this logic automatically.\n    42→*   **Streaming Watches:** A `WATCH` request returns a `watch.Interface` (from\n    43→    `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/watch`), which provides a channel of structured `watch.Event`\n    44→    objects (`ADDED`, `MODIFIED`, `DELETED`, `BOOKMARK`). This decouples the watch consumer from\n    45→    the underlying streaming protocol.\n    46→\n    47→### Errors, Warnings, and Rate Limiting\n    48→\n    49→*   **Structured Errors:** The client deserializes non-2xx responses into a structured\n    50→    `errors.StatusError`, enabling programmatic error handling (e.g., `errors.IsNotFound(err)`).\n    51→*   **Warnings:** It processes non-fatal `Warning` headers from the API server via a\n    52→    `WarningHandler`.\n    53→*   **Client-Side Rate Limiting:** The `QPS` and `Burst` settings in `rest.Config` are the\n    54→    client's half of the contract with the server's API Priority and Fairness system.\n    55→*   **Server-Side Throttling:** The client's default transport automatically handles HTTP `429`\n    56→    responses by reading the `Retry-After` header, waiting, and retrying the request.\n    57→\n    58→## Typed and Dynamic Clients\n    59→\n    60→To handle the extensible nature of the Kubernetes API, `client-go` provides two primary client\n    61→models.\n    62→\n    63→The **`kubernetes.Clientset`** provides compile-time, type-safe access to core, built-in APIs.\n    64→\n    65→The **`dynamic.DynamicClient`** represents all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured`, allowing it\n    66→to interact with any API resource, including CRDs. It relies on two discovery mechanisms:\n    67→1.  The **`discovery.DiscoveryClient`** determines *what* resources exist. The\n    68→    **`CachedDiscoveryClient`** is an optimization that caches this data on disk to solve.\n    69→2.  The **OpenAPI schema** (fetched from `/openapi/v3`) describes the *structure* of those\n    70→    resources, providing the schema awareness needed by the dynamic client.\n    71→\n    72→## Code Generation\n    73→\n    74→A core architectural principle of `client-go` is the use of code generation to provide a\n    75→strongly-typed, compile-time-safe interface for specific API GroupVersions. This makes\n    76→controller code more robust and easier to maintain. The tools in `k8s.io/code-generator` produce\n    77→several key components:\n    78→\n    79→*   **Typed Clientsets:** The primary interface for interacting with a specific GroupVersion.\n    80→*   **Typed Listers:** The read-only, cached accessors used by controllers.\n    81→*   **Typed Informers:** The machinery for populating the cache for a specific type.\n    82→*   **Apply Configurations:** The type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply.\n    83→\n    84→A contributor modifying a built-in API type **must** run the code generation scripts to update all\n    85→of these dependent components. For the Kubernetes project, `hack/update-codegen.sh` runs code generation.\n    86→\n    87→`sample-controller` shows how code generate can be configured to build custom controllers.\n    88→\n    89→## Controller Infrastructure\n    90→\n    91→The `tools/cache` package provides the core infrastructure for controllers, replacing a high-load,\n    92→request-based pattern with a low-load, event-driven, cached model.\n    93→\n    94→The data flow is as follows:\n    95→\n    96→```mermaid\n    97→graph TD\n    98→    subgraph \"Kubernetes API\"\n    99→        API_Server[API Server]\n   100→    end\n   101→\n   102→    subgraph \"client-go: Informer Mechanism\"\n   103→        Reflector(\"1. Reflector\")\n   104→        DeltaFIFO(\"2. DeltaFIFO\")\n   105→        Indexer[\"3. Indexer (Cache)\"]\n   106→        EventHandlers(\"4. Event Handlers\")\n   107→    end\n   108→\n   109→    subgraph \"User Code\"\n   110→        WorkQueue[\"5. Work Queue\"]\n   111→        Controller(\"6. Controller\")\n   112→    end\n   113→\n   114→    API_Server -- LIST/WATCH --> Reflector\n   115→    Reflector -- Puts changes into --> DeltaFIFO\n   116→    DeltaFIFO -- Is popped by internal loop, which updates --> Indexer\n   117→    Indexer -- Update triggers --> EventHandlers\n   118→    EventHandlers -- Adds key to --> WorkQueue\n   119→    WorkQueue -- Is processed by --> Controller\n   120→    Controller -- Reads from cache via Lister --> Indexer\n   121→```\n   122→\n   123→A **`Reflector`** performs a `LIST` to get a consistent snapshot of a resource, identified by a\n   124→`resourceVersion`. It then starts a `WATCH` from that `resourceVersion` to receive a continuous\n   125→stream of subsequent changes. The `Reflector`'s relist/rewatch loop is designed to solve the\n   126→**\"too old\" `resourceVersion` error** by re-listing. To make this recovery more efficient, the\n   127→`Reflector` consumes **watch bookmarks** from the server, which provide a more recent\n   128→`resourceVersion` to restart from.\n   129→\n   130→The **`Lister`** is the primary, read-only, thread-safe interface for a controller's business\n   131→logic to access the `Indexer`'s cache.\n   132→\n   133→## Controller Patterns\n   134→\n   135→The controller infrastructure is architecturally decoupled from the controller's business logic to\n   136→ensure resiliency.\n   137→\n   138→The **`util/workqueue`** creates a critical boundary between event detection (the informer's job)\n   139→and reconciliation (the controller's job). Informer event handlers only add an object's key to the\n   140→work queue. This allows the controller to retry failed operations with exponential backoff without\n   141→blocking the informer's watch stream.\n   142→\n   143→For high availability, the **`tools/leaderelection`** package provides the standard architectural\n   144→solution to ensure single-writer semantics by having replicas compete to acquire a lock on a\n   145→shared `Lease` object.\n   146→\n   147→## Server-Side Apply\n   148→\n   149→`client-go` provides a distinct architectural pattern for object mutation that aligns with the\n   150→server's declarative model. This is a separate workflow from the traditional `get-modify-update`\n   151→model that allows multiple controllers to safely co-manage the same object. The\n   152→**`applyconfigurations`** package provides the generated, type-safe builder API used to\n   153→construct the declarative patch.\n   154→\n   155→## Versioning and Compatibility\n   156→\n   157→`client-go` has a strict versioning relationship with the main Kubernetes repository. A `client-go`\n   158→version `v0.X.Y` corresponds to the Kubernetes version `v1.X.Y`.\n   159→\n   160→The Kubernetes API has strong backward compatibility guarantees: a client built with an older\n   161→version of `client-go` will work with a newer API server. However, the reverse is not guaranteed.\n   162→A contributor must not break compatibility with supported versions of the Kubernetes API server.\n   163→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. It describes the\nmajor components, how they interact, and the key design decisions that shape the library.\n\n## Client Configuration\n\nThere is an architectural separation between loading client configuration and using it. The\n`rest.Config` object is the in-memory representation of this configuration. The\n`tools/clientcmd` package is the standard factory for producing it. `clientcmd` handles the\ncomplex logic of parsing `kubeconfig` files, merging contexts, and handling external\nauthentication providers (e.g., OIDC).\n\n## REST Client\n\nThe `rest.Client` is the foundational HTTP client that underpins all other clients. It separates\nthe low-level concerns of HTTP transport, serialization, and error handling from higher-level,\nKubernetes-specific object logic.\n\nThe `rest.Config` object is used to build the underlying HTTP transport, which is typically a\nchain of `http.RoundTripper` objects. Each element in the chain is responsible for a specific\ntask, such as adding an `Authorization` header. This is the mechanism by which all authentication\nis injected into requests.\n\nThe client uses a builder pattern for requests (e.g., `.Verb()`, `.Resource()`), deferring\nresponse processing until a method like `.Into(&pod)` is called. This separation is key to\nsupporting different client models from a common base.\n\n### Endpoint Interactions\n\n*   **Content Negotiation:** The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate the wire format\n    (JSON or Protobuf). A key performance optimization using this mechanism is the ability to\n    request metadata-only objects via the `as=PartialObjectMetadata;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameter.\n    Also the `as=Table;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameters may be used to request lists as tables. \n*   **Subresources:** The client can target standard subresources like `/status` or `/scale` for\n    object mutations, and it can also handle action-oriented subresources like `/logs` or\n    `/exec`, which often involve streaming data.\n*   **List Pagination:** For `LIST` requests, the client can specify a `limit`. The server will\n    return up to that many items and, if more exist, a `continue` token. The client is\n    responsible for passing this token in a subsequent request to retrieve the next page.\n    Higher-level tools like the `Reflector`'s `ListerWatcher` handle this logic automatically.\n*   **Streaming Watches:** A `WATCH` request returns a `watch.Interface` (from\n    `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/watch`), which provides a channel of structured `watch.Event`\n    objects (`ADDED`, `MODIFIED`, `DELETED`, `BOOKMARK`). This decouples the watch consumer from\n    the underlying streaming protocol.\n\n### Errors, Warnings, and Rate Limiting\n\n*   **Structured Errors:** The client deserializes non-2xx responses into a structured\n    `errors.StatusError`, enabling programmatic error handling (e.g., `errors.IsNotFound(err)`).\n*   **Warnings:** It processes non-fatal `Warning` headers from the API server via a\n    `WarningHandler`.\n*   **Client-Side Rate Limiting:** The `QPS` and `Burst` settings in `rest.Config` are the\n    client's half of the contract with the server's API Priority and Fairness system.\n*   **Server-Side Throttling:** The client's default transport automatically handles HTTP `429`\n    responses by reading the `Retry-After` header, waiting, and retrying the request.\n\n## Typed and Dynamic Clients\n\nTo handle the extensible nature of the Kubernetes API, `client-go` provides two primary client\nmodels.\n\nThe **`kubernetes.Clientset`** provides compile-time, type-safe access to core, built-in APIs.\n\nThe **`dynamic.DynamicClient`** represents all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured`, allowing it\nto interact with any API resource, including CRDs. It relies on two discovery mechanisms:\n1.  The **`discovery.DiscoveryClient`** determines *what* resources exist. The\n    **`CachedDiscoveryClient`** is an optimization that caches this data on disk to solve.\n2.  The **OpenAPI schema** (fetched from `/openapi/v3`) describes the *structure* of those\n    resources, providing the schema awareness needed by the dynamic client.\n\n## Code Generation\n\nA core architectural principle of `client-go` is the use of code generation to provide a\nstrongly-typed, compile-time-safe interface for specific API GroupVersions. This makes\ncontroller code more robust and easier to maintain. The tools in `k8s.io/code-generator` produce\nseveral key components:\n\n*   **Typed Clientsets:** The primary interface for interacting with a specific GroupVersion.\n*   **Typed Listers:** The read-only, cached accessors used by controllers.\n*   **Typed Informers:** The machinery for populating the cache for a specific type.\n*   **Apply Configurations:** The type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply.\n\nA contributor modifying a built-in API type **must** run the code generation scripts to update all\nof these dependent components. For the Kubernetes project, `hack/update-codegen.sh` runs code generation.\n\n`sample-controller` shows how code generate can be configured to build custom controllers.\n\n## Controller Infrastructure\n\nThe `tools/cache` package provides the core infrastructure for controllers, replacing a high-load,\nrequest-based pattern with a low-load, event-driven, cached model.\n\nThe data flow is as follows:\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph \"Kubernetes API\"\n        API_Server[API Server]\n    end\n\n    subgraph \"client-go: Informer Mechanism\"\n        Reflector(\"1. Reflector\")\n        DeltaFIFO(\"2. DeltaFIFO\")\n        Indexer[\"3. Indexer (Cache)\"]\n        EventHandlers(\"4. Event Handlers\")\n    end\n\n    subgraph \"User Code\"\n        WorkQueue[\"5. Work Queue\"]\n        Controller(\"6. Controller\")\n    end\n\n    API_Server -- LIST/WATCH --> Reflector\n    Reflector -- Puts changes into --> DeltaFIFO\n    DeltaFIFO -- Is popped by internal loop, which updates --> Indexer\n    Indexer -- Update triggers --> EventHandlers\n    EventHandlers -- Adds key to --> WorkQueue\n    WorkQueue -- Is processed by --> Controller\n    Controller -- Reads from cache via Lister --> Indexer\n```\n\nA **`Reflector`** performs a `LIST` to get a consistent snapshot of a resource, identified by a\n`resourceVersion`. It then starts a `WATCH` from that `resourceVersion` to receive a continuous\nstream of subsequent changes. The `Reflector`'s relist/rewatch loop is designed to solve the\n**\"too old\" `resourceVersion` error** by re-listing. To make this recovery more efficient, the\n`Reflector` consumes **watch bookmarks** from the server, which provide a more recent\n`resourceVersion` to restart from.\n\nThe **`Lister`** is the primary, read-only, thread-safe interface for a controller's business\nlogic to access the `Indexer`'s cache.\n\n## Controller Patterns\n\nThe controller infrastructure is architecturally decoupled from the controller's business logic to\nensure resiliency.\n\nThe **`util/workqueue`** creates a critical boundary between event detection (the informer's job)\nand reconciliation (the controller's job). Informer event handlers only add an object's key to the\nwork queue. This allows the controller to retry failed operations with exponential backoff without\nblocking the informer's watch stream.\n\nFor high availability, the **`tools/leaderelection`** package provides the standard architectural\nsolution to ensure single-writer semantics by having replicas compete to acquire a lock on a\nshared `Lease` object.\n\n## Server-Side Apply\n\n`client-go` provides a distinct architectural pattern for object mutation that aligns with the\nserver's declarative model. This is a separate workflow from the traditional `get-modify-update`\nmodel that allows multiple controllers to safely co-manage the same object. The\n**`applyconfigurations`** package provides the generated, type-safe builder API used to\nconstruct the declarative patch.\n\n## Versioning and Compatibility\n\n`client-go` has a strict versioning relationship with the main Kubernetes repository. A `client-go`\nversion `v0.X.Y` corresponds to the Kubernetes version `v1.X.Y`.\n\nThe Kubernetes API has strong backward compatibility guarantees: a client built with an older\nversion of `client-go` will work with a newer API server. However, the reverse is not guaranteed.\nA contributor must not break compatibility with supported versions of the Kubernetes API server.\n","numLines":163,"startLine":1,"totalLines":163}}}

PRs that are\n    50→cherry-picked into an older Kubernetes release branch will result in an update\n    51→to the corresponding branch in `client-go`, with a corresponding new tag\n    52→changing the patch version.\n    53→\n    54→#### Branches and tags.\n    55→\n    56→We will create a new branch and tag for each increment in the minor version\n    57→number. We will create only a new tag for each increment in the patch\n    58→version number. See [semver](http://semver.org/) for definitions of major,\n    59→minor, and patch.\n    60→\n    61→The HEAD of the master branch in client-go will track the HEAD of the master\n    62→branch in the main Kubernetes repo.\n    63→\n    64→#### Compatibility: your code <-> client-go\n    65→\n    66→The `v0.x.y` tags indicate that go APIs may change in incompatible ways in\n    67→different 73→\n    74→Since Kubernetes is backwards compatible with clients, older `client-go`\n    75→versions will work with many different Kubernetes cluster versions.\n    76→\n    77→We will backport bugfixes--but not new features--into older versions of\n    78→`client-go`.\n    79→\n    80→\n    81→#### Compatibility matrix\n    82→\n    83→|                               | Kubernetes 1.29 | (E.g., the clock for the release-2.0 branch started ticking when we\n   134→tagged v2.0.0, not when we made the first alpha.) This policy applies to\n   135→every version greater than or equal to 2.0.\n   136→\n   137→#### Why do the 1.4 and 1.5 branch contain top-level folder named after the version?\n   138→\n   139→For the initial release of client-go, we thought it would be easiest to keep\n   140→separate directories for each minor version. That soon proved to be a mistake.\n   141→We are keeping the top-level folders in the 1.4 and 1.5 branches so that\n   142→existing users won't be broken.\n   143→\n   144→### Kubernetes tags\n   145→\n   146→This repository is still a mirror of\n   147→[k8s.io/kubernetes/staging/src/client-go](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/tree/master/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go),\n   148→the code development is still done in the staging area.\n   149→\n   150→Since Kubernetes `v1.8.0`, when syncing the code from the staging area,\n   151→we also sync the Kubernetes version tags to client-go, prefixed with\n   152→`kubernetes-`. From Kubernetes `v1.17.0`, we also create matching semver\n   153→`v0.x.y` tags for each `v1.x.y` Kubernetes release.\n   154→\n   155→For example, if you check out the `kubernetes-1.17.0` or the `v0.17.0` tag in\n   156→client-go, the code you get is exactly the same as if you check out the `v1.17.0`\n   157→tag in Kubernetes, and change directory to `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go`.\n   158→\n   159→The purpose is to let users quickly find matching commits among published repos,\n   160→like [sample-apiserver](https://github.com/kubernetes/sample-apiserver),\n   161→[apiextension-apiserver](https://github.com/kubernetes/apiextensions-apiserver),\n   162→etc. The Kubernetes version tag does NOT claim any backwards compatibility\n   163→guarantees for client-go. For example:\n   169→\n   170→```\n   171→go get k8s.io/client-go@latest\n   172→```\n   173→\n   174→To get a specific version, use go1.11+ and fetch the desired version using the `go get` command. For example:\n   175→\n   176→```\n   177→go get k8s.io/client-go@v0.20.4\n   178→```\n   179→\n   180→See [INSTALL.md](/INSTALL.md) for detailed instructions and troubleshooting.\n   181→\n   182→### How to use it\n   183→\n   184→If your application runs in a Pod in the cluster, please refer to the\n   185→in-cluster [example](examples/in-cluster-client-configuration), otherwise please\n   186→refer to the out-of-cluster [example](examples/out-of-cluster-client-configuration).\n   187→\n   188→### Dependency management\n   189→\n   190→For details on how to correctly use a dependency management for installing client-go, please see [INSTALL.md](INSTALL.md).\n   191→\n   192→### Contributing code\n   193→Please send pull requests against the client packages in the Kubernetes main [repository](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes). We will create only a new tag for each increment in the patch\nversion number. repo.\n\n#### Compatibility: your code <-> client-go\n\nThe `v0.x.y` tags indicate that go APIs may change in incompatible ways in\ndifferent versions.\n\nSee [INSTALL.md](INSTALL.md) for guidelines on requiring a specific\nversion of client-go.\n\n#### Compatibility: client-go <-> Kubernetes clusters\n\nSince Kubernetes is backwards compatible with clients, older `client-go`\nversions will work All are\n    32→// optional.\n    33→type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\n    34→\n    35→\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\n    36→\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\n    37→\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\n    38→\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n    39→\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\n    40→\n    41→\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\n    42→\t// this queue \"knows about\". It is used to decide which items are missing\n    43→\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n    44→\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n    45→\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n    46→\n    47→\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n    48→\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\n    49→\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\n    50→\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\n    51→\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\n    52→\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\n    53→\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n    54→\n    55→\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\n    56→\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\n    57→\tTransformer TransformFunc\n    58→\n    59→\t// If set, log output will go to this logger instead of klog.Background().\n    60→\tLogger *klog.Logger\n    61→}\n    62→\n    63→// DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\n    64→// accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n    65→// but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n    66→// object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n    67→// except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n    68→// Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n    69→// not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n    70→// Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n    71→// DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n    72→//\n    73→// The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n    74→// an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n    75→// If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n    76→// replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n    77→// resync events.\n    78→//\n    79→// DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n    80→// intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n    81→// the Pop() method.\n    82→//\n    83→// DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n    84→//   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n    85→//   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n    86→//     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n    87→//   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n    88→//   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n    89→//\n    90→// DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n    91→// interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n    92→// will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n    93→// the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n    94→//\n    95→// A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n    96→// to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n    97→// question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n    98→// modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n    99→// (each in a different way).\n   100→//\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. All are\n// optional.\ntype DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\n\n\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\n\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\n\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\n\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\n\n\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\n\t// this queue \"knows about\". It is used to decide which items are missing\n\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n\n\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\n\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\n\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\n\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\n\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\n\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n\n\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\n\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\n\tTransformer TransformFunc\n\n\t// If set, log output will go to this logger instead of klog.Background().\n\tLogger *klog.Logger\n}\n\n// DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\n// accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n// but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n// object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n// except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n// Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n// not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n// Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n//\n// The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n// an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n// If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n// replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n// resync events.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n// intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n// the Pop() method.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n//   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n//   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n//     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n//   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n//   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n// interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n// will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n// the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n//\n// A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n// to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n// question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n// modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n// (each in a different way).\n//","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":746}}}

This may be\n\t// useful if the implementation allows priority change for the given item.\n\tTouch(item T)\n\t// Push adds a new item.\n\tPush(item T)\n\t// Len tells the total number of items.\n\tLen() int\n\t// Pop retrieves an item.\n\tPop() (item T)\n}\n\n// DefaultQueue is a slice based FIFO queue.\nfunc DefaultQueue[T comparable]() Queue[T] {\n\treturn new(queue[T])\n}\n\n// queue is a slice which implements Queue.\ntype queue[T comparable] []T\n\nfunc (q *queue[T]) Touch(item T) {}\n\nfunc (q *queue[T]) Push(item T) {\n\t*q = append(*q, item)\n}\n\nfunc (q *queue[T]) Len() int {\n\treturn len(*q)\n}\n\nfunc (q *queue[T]) Pop() (item T) {\n\titem = (*q)[0]\n\n\t// The underlying array still exists and reference this object, so the object will not be garbage collected.\n\t(*q)[0] = *new(T)\n\t*q = (*q)[1:]\n\n\treturn item\n}\n\n// QueueConfig specifies optional configurations to customize an Interface.\n// Deprecated: use TypedQueueConfig instead.\ntype QueueConfig = TypedQueueConfig[any]\n\ntype TypedQueueConfig[T comparable] struct {\n\t// Name for the queue. If unnamed, the metrics will not be registered.\n\tName string\n\n\t// MetricsProvider optionally allows specifying a metrics provider to use for the queue\n\t// instead of the global provider.\n\tMetricsProvider MetricsProvider\n\n\t// Clock ability to inject real or fake clock for testing purposes.\n\tClock clock.WithTicker\n\n\t// Queue provides the underlying queue to use. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01KaZ1ZTYnLBmu76vQoYCAez","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_017rNSjcUC4rbHhGBuhfBy8A","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes client-go Systems Guide\n\n## Overview\n\n`client-go` is the foundational Go library for programmatic interaction with Kubernetes clusters. It provides multiple abstraction layers to support diverse use cases—from simple CLI tools to complex controllers managing distributed systems. The subsystem is architecturally designed to balance type safety, performance, extensibility, and operational resilience.\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nclient-go serves as the canonical interface for Go programs to:\n- **Query and mutate** Kubernetes API objects (pods, deployments, custom resources, etc.)\n- **Watch** cluster state changes in real-time\n- **Discover** available APIs and their schemas\n- **Cache** API state locally with automatic synchronization\n- **Coordinate** multi-replica controllers via leader election\n- **Handle authentication**, authorization, and transport layer security\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream (dependencies):**\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery`: Core runtime objects (ObjectMeta, TypeMeta, runtime.Object), watch interfaces, and versioning primitives\n- `k8s.io/api`: Generated type definitions for all Kubernetes API resources (Pod, Deployment, etc.)\n- `k8s.io/utils`, `k8s.io/klog`: Utility libraries (time management, logging, sets)\n- Standard library: `net/http`, `encoding/json`, `crypto/tls`\n\n**Downstream (consumers):**\n- **Controllers**: Operators, custom controllers that reconcile cluster state\n- **CLI tools**: kubectl (internally uses client-go)\n- **Webhooks**: Admission controllers, mutating/validating webhooks\n- **Monitoring/observability**: Custom metrics collectors, log aggregators\n- **End-user applications**: Any program that needs Kubernetes integration\n\n### Scope and Separation of Concerns\n\nclient-go does **not**:\n- Generate or manage Kubernetes API objects themselves (that's `k8s.io/api` via code-gen)\n- Provide control plane functionality (that's kube-apiserver's job)\n- Handle specific business logic for controller reconciliation patterns (that's the consumer's responsibility)\n- Enforce cluster-wide ordering guarantees (watch events may arrive out-of-order; the consumer must handle this)\n\nclient-go **does**:\n- Manage HTTP transport, authentication, and TLS\n- Serialize/deserialize Kubernetes objects (JSON, Protobuf, CBOR)\n- Maintain an in-process cache synchronized via watch\n- Provide rate limiting and exponential backoff\n- Support both typed (generated code) and untyped (dynamic) access\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nclient-go is organized into several tightly integrated subsystems:\n\n### 2.1 REST Foundation (`rest/` package)\n\n**Responsibility:** Low-level HTTP client and configuration management.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `rest/config.go`: `Config` struct holding credentials, API server URL, TLS settings, rate limits\n- `rest/client.go`: `RESTClient` implementing verb-based request builder pattern (e.g., `.Get().Resource(\"pods\").Into(&pod)`)\n- `rest/request.go`: Request pipeline—constructs URLs, handles serialization, error parsing\n- `rest/transport.go`: HTTP round-tripper composition for authentication, compression, retry logic\n- `rest/with_retry.go`: Exponential backoff with jitter for transient failures\n\n**Design Pattern:**\n- **Builder pattern** for requests: `.Verb(\"GET\").Namespace(\"default\").Resource(\"pods\").Name(\"my-pod\").Do(ctx)` defers I/O until terminal method is invoked\n- **RoundTripper chain**: Authentication, rate limiting, warning handler, and compression are injected as middleware layers\n- **Content negotiation**: Accept headers (JSON, Protobuf, CBOR, metadata-only) allow clients to optimize wire format per request\n\n**Example Request Flow:**\n```\nRESTClient.Get()\n  → *Request (builder object, no I/O yet)\n  → .Namespace(\"default\")\n  → .Resource(\"pods\")\n  → .Name(\"my-pod\")\n  → .Do(ctx)  ← actual HTTP call via transport chain\n```\n\n### 2.2 Configuration and Authentication (`rest/config.go`, `tools/clientcmd/`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Load credentials and cluster endpoints from kubeconfig files or in-cluster service accounts.\n\n**Key Abstractions:**\n- `rest.Config`: Immutable configuration object (host, TLS certs, bearer token, rate limits)\n  - `QPS`: Requests per second (default 5)\n  - `Burst`: Burst capacity above sustained QPS (default 10)\n  - `WrapTransport`: Hook for custom middleware\n- `rest.InClusterConfig()`: Reads `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/{token,ca.crt}` and `KUBERNETES_SERVICE_HOST` environment variables\n- `clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags()`: Parses `~/.kube/config`, merges contexts, handles external auth providers (OIDC, exec-based)\n\n**Separation of Concerns:**\n- Configuration **loading** is intentionally separated from **usage**, allowing decoupling of kubeconfig parsing logic from client code\n- Auth providers (exec-based, plugin-based) are pluggable via `AuthProviderConfig` and `ExecConfig`\n- TLS mutual authentication is configured at the REST transport level, not at the Kubernetes object level\n\n### 2.3 Client Models: Typed vs. Dynamic\n\nclient-go provides two complementary client models:\n\n#### 2.3.1 Typed Client (`kubernetes.Clientset`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Compile-time type-safe access to core and built-in API resources.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `kubernetes/clientset.go`: Aggregates clients for all API groups and versions\n- `kubernetes/typed/core/v1/pod.go` (auto-generated): Interface `PodsGetter` with `Pods(namespace string) PodInterface`\n- Generated via `k8s.io/code-generator`: code-gen tools produce strongly-typed interfaces for each API GroupVersion\n\n**Design:**\n- Each API group version (e.g., `apps/v1`, `batch/v1`) has a generated client\n- Namespace-scoped and cluster-scoped resources are differentiated at the interface level\n- Subresources (`/status`, `/scale`) are exposed as separate methods\n\n**Usage Example:**\n```go\nclientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", metav1.GetOptions{})\nclientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Update(ctx, deployment, metav1.UpdateOptions{})\n```\n\n**Limitation:** Requires code generation for new API types; cannot access CRDs without additional code generation\n\n#### 2.3.2 Dynamic Client (`dynamic.DynamicClient`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Runtime-polymorphic access to any API resource (including CRDs) using `unstructured.Unstructured`.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `dynamic/simple.go`: `DynamicClient` wraps a `rest.Interface`\n- `dynamic/interface.go`: `Resource()` method returns a `ResourceInterface` for any GVR (GroupVersionResource)\n\n**Design:**\n- Works with any API resource without code generation\n- Operates on untyped JSON/CBOR maps: `.Get()` returns `*unstructured.Unstructured`\n- Relies on discovery to determine namespace scope, subresources, etc.\n\n**Usage Example:**\n```go\ndynClient := dynamic.NewForConfig(config)\ngvr := schema.GroupVersionResource{Group: \"example.com\", Version: \"v1\", Resource: \"foos\"}\nobj, err := dynClient.Resource(gvr).Namespace(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-foo\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n// obj is *unstructured.Unstructured\n```\n\n**Trade-offs:**\n- **Pro:** Immediate support for any new API type (including CRDs)\n- **Con:** No compile-time type checking; schema validation is deferred to runtime via OpenAPI spec\n\n### 2.4 Discovery (`discovery/` package)\n\n**Responsibility:** Determine which APIs exist on the cluster and their structure.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `discovery/discovery_client.go`: `DiscoveryClient` queries `/api`, `/apis`, `/openapi/v3`\n- `discovery/cached/disk/cached_discovery.go`: Caches discovery data on disk (e.g., `~/.kube/cache/discovery`)\n- `discovery/aggregated_discovery.go`: Implements newer aggregated discovery format (APIGroupDiscoveryList)\n\n**Three Discovery Mechanisms:**\n1. **Legacy Discovery** (`ServerGroups()`, `ServerResourcesForGroupVersion()`)\n   - Lightweight: returns list of groups and their resources\n   - No schema information; used primarily by `dynamic` client to determine namespace scope\n2. **OpenAPI v2** (deprecated): Full JSON schema via `/openapi/v2`\n3. **OpenAPI v3** (preferred): Modular JSON schemas via `/openapi/v3/{group}/{version}/...`\n\n**Failure Handling:**\n- Caching solves the \"cluster unreachable\" problem for tools that cached discovery data\n- Disk cache allows kubectl to function even when API server is temporarily unavailable\n- Aggregated discovery (v2) streams all information in one request, reducing round-trips\n\n**Usage in Practice:**\n- `dynamic.DynamicClient` calls discovery to determine if a resource is namespaced\n- Tools like kubectl use discovery to populate CLI completion and validate resource types\n- Controllers typically **don't** use discovery at runtime; they use pre-generated, compile-time-known types\n\n### 2.5 Controller Infrastructure (`tools/cache/` package)\n\n**Responsibility:** Provide an event-driven, cached model for watching cluster state changes.\n\n**Key Components:**\n\n#### 2.5.1 Reflector (`tools/cache/reflector.go`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Synchronize a local cache with the API server's authoritative state.\n\n**Design:**\n1. Performs a **LIST** to snapshot all current objects (identified by `resourceVersion`)\n2. Starts a **WATCH** from that `resourceVersion` to receive subsequent changes\n3. Handles the \"too old resourceVersion\" error by re-listing with exponential backoff\n4. Consumes watch bookmarks to advance the restart point without re-listing\n\n**Key Parameters:**\n- `minWatchTimeout` (default 5min): Minimum timeout for watch requests to spread load\n- `resyncPeriod`: Periodic re-list frequency (e.g., 10 minutes for informers)\n- `WatchListPageSize`: Request pagination during initial list and re-list\n\n**Failure Modes:**\n- **\"Too old resourceVersion\"**: Watch stream is too stale; Reflector must re-list. Bookmarks reduce cost.\n- **Network partition**: Watch connection dropped; exponential backoff before retry\n- **API server restarts**: Watch stream terminates; Reflector automatically resumes\n\n#### 2.5.2 DeltaFIFO (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Queue of object deltas that preserves the sequence of changes for each object.\n\n**Key Insight:**\n- Unlike a simple FIFO (which stores objects), DeltaFIFO stores `Deltas` (slice of changes)\n- Example: `pod1: [Added, Modified, Modified, Deleted]`\n- Allows the consumer to replay the entire history of changes without losing intermediate states\n\n**Delta Types:**\n- `Added`: Object appeared in LIST or WATCH ADDED event\n- `Updated`: Object was mutated (WATCH MODIFIED event)\n- `Deleted`: Object was removed\n- `Replaced`: Result of a LIST operation (if `EmitDeltaTypeReplaced` is true)\n- `Sync`: Resync operation (periodic re-processing)\n\n**Usage:**\n- Reflector **pushes** object changes into DeltaFIFO\n- Controller **pops** deltas and processes them sequentially\n- Deduplication: If last delta is `Deleted` and new delta is also `Deleted`, the FIFO doesn't grow\n\n#### 2.5.3 Indexer (Thread-safe Cache) (`tools/cache/store.go`, `tools/cache/index.go`)\n\n**Responsibility:** In-memory, thread-safe store of objects with secondary indices for efficient queries.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `tools/cache/store.go`: `Store` interface and `cache` implementation\n- `tools/cache/index.go`: `Indexer` interface with `Index()`, `IndexKeys()`, `ByIndex()` methods\n\n**Features:**\n- **Thread-safe**: RWMutex guards reads and writes\n- **Secondary indices**: Index by namespace, owner references, labels, or custom functions\n- **Efficient queries**: `ByIndex(\"namespace\", \"default\")` returns all objects in that namespace without full scan\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nindexer.Add(pod)  // pod added to cache\nindexer.ByIndex(\"namespace\", \"default\")  // O(1) lookup via index\n```\n\n#### 2.5.4 Event Handlers and Informer Pattern\n\n**Responsibility:** Notify consumers of object changes and manage event ordering.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `tools/cache/shared_informer.go`: `SharedInformer` aggregates event listeners\n- `tools/cache/controller.go`: `Config` and `Run()` orchestrating the full flow\n\n**Event Handler Pattern:**\n```go\nhandler := cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n  AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) { workQueue.Add(obj) },\n  UpdateFunc: func(oldObj, newObj interface{}) { workQueue.Add(newObj) },\n  DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) { workQueue.Add(obj) },\n}\ninformer.AddEventHandler(handler)\n```\n\n**Design Principle:** Event handlers **must not perform expensive operations**. They add work items to a queue; the controller processes items from the queue with retries and backoff.\n\n### 2.6 Work Queue (`util/workqueue/`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Decouple event detection from business logic processing.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `util/workqueue/queue.go`: `Interface` (Add, Get, Done, Len)\n- `util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go`: `DelayingInterface` (AddAfter)\n- `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go`: `RateLimitingInterface` (AddRateLimited)\n- `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go`: Built-in rate limiters (exponential backoff, max retries)\n\n**Responsibilities Separated:**\n1. **Detection**: Informer handler adds a work item (e.g., \"default/my-pod\")\n2. **Queueing**: Item waits in the work queue\n3. **Processing**: Controller worker pops item, processes it, calls `Done()` on success or `AddRateLimited()` on failure\n4. **Rate Limiting**: Failed items are re-queued with exponential backoff\n\n**Design:**\n- Work queue stores **keys** (e.g., \"namespace/name\"), not full objects\n- Controller fetches the object from cache (via Lister) when processing the key\n- If object is not in cache (deleted), controller handles the \"not found\" gracefully\n\n**Example Retry Flow:**\n```\nItem \"default/pod1\" fails to reconcile\n→ workqueue.AddRateLimited(\"default/pod1\")  // exponential backoff\n→ 2 seconds later, item re-queued\n→ 4 seconds later, if failed again\n→ 8 seconds later, if failed again\n→ Max retries reached (or max duration), item dropped\n```\n\n### 2.7 Listers (`listers/` and `informers/` packages)\n\n**Responsibility:** Provide read-only, type-safe access to the cache for controllers.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `listers/core/v1/pod_lister.go` (auto-generated): Interface with methods like `Pods(namespace string) PodNamespaceLister`\n- `informers/core/v1/pod.go` (auto-generated): `PodInformer` with `Lister()` method returning a `PodLister`\n\n**Design:**\n- Generated from API types via code-gen\n- Lister implements `ByIndex()`, `List()` with field selectors\n- Controller never calls `.Get()` directly on the client; it uses the Lister for cached access\n\n**Usage:**\n```go\npodLister := podInformer.Lister()\npod, err := podLister.Pods(\"default\").Get(\"my-pod\")  // cache lookup, no API call\npods, err := podLister.Pods(\"default\").List(selector)  // filtered cache lookup\n```\n\n### 2.8 Server-Side Apply (`applyconfigurations/`, `util/apply/`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Provide a declarative, merge-aware API for object mutation that allows multiple controllers to co-manage the same object.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment_applyconfiguration.go` (auto-generated): Type-safe builder API\n- `util/apply/apply.go`: Helper functions for constructing apply patches\n\n**Contrast with Traditional Update:**\n- **Traditional GET-MODIFY-UPDATE**: Retrieve object → mutate fields → UPDATE. Requires **exclusive ownership**.\n- **Server-Side Apply (kubectl apply -f)**: Send desired state + fieldManager → server merges with other managers. Allows **shared ownership**.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\n// Traditional: risky if someone else modified the object\ndeployment, _ := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-app\", metav1.GetOptions{})\ndeployment.Spec.Replicas = ptr.To(int32(3))\nclientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Update(ctx, deployment, metav1.UpdateOptions{})\n\n// Server-Side Apply: safe for shared ownership\ndeploymentAC := appsv1ac.Deployment(\"my-app\", \"default\").\n  WithSpec(appsv1ac.DeploymentSpec().WithReplicas(3))\nclientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Apply(ctx, deploymentAC, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"})\n```\n\n### 2.9 Leader Election (`tools/leaderelection/`)\n\n**Responsibility:** Ensure only one controller replica actively reconciles at a time.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`: `LeaderElector` with `Run(ctx)` method\n- `tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/lease.go`: Uses `coordination.k8s.io/v1/Lease` objects for locking\n\n**Design:**\n- All replicas compete for a lock on a shared `Lease` object\n- Lock holder periodically renews; if renewal fails, lock is released and another replica can acquire\n- OnNewLeader and OnStoppedLeading callbacks let controller start/stop reconciliation\n\n**Example Flow:**\n```\nReplica-1, Replica-2, Replica-3 all running\n→ All try to acquire lock on \"my-controller-lock\" Lease\n→ Replica-2 succeeds: becomes leader\n→ Replica-2 renews lock every `renewDeadline`\n→ Replica-2 crashes\n→ Lock expires after `leaseDuration`\n→ Replica-3 acquires lock: becomes new leader\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Configuration to Client Creation\n\n```\nUser's kubeconfig file (~/.kube/config)\n  ↓\nclientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags(\"\", kubeconfigPath)\n  → Parses YAML, merges contexts\n  → Loads certs, token, auth provider config\n  → Returns rest.Config (immutable)\n  ↓\nkubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\n  → Creates rest.Client for each API group\n  → Wraps in Clientset interface\n  ↓\nClientset ready for API calls\n  e.g., clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n```\n\n**Evidence:** `rest/config.go:432-500` (BuildConfig and BuildConfigFromFlags), `kubernetes/clientset.go` (Clientset constructor)\n\n### 3.2 A Single API Request\n\n```\nuser code: clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n  ↓\nrest.Client.Get().Namespace(\"default\").Resource(\"pods\").Name(\"my-pod\").Do(ctx)\n  ↓\n(*Request).Do(ctx) [rest/request.go:515]\n  1. Build URL: \"https://api-server/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/my-pod\"\n  2. Set headers: Accept, Content-Type, Authorization (from transport chain)\n  3. http.Client.Do(request)\n  ↓\nTransport RoundTripper chain [rest/transport.go]:\n  1. WrapTransport middleware (if configured)\n  2. TLS config + client certs\n  3. Authorization header injection (bearer token, basic auth, exec provider)\n  4. Rate limiter (check QPS/Burst quota)\n  5. Actual http.RoundTripper (net/http internal)\n  6. On 429 (Too Many Requests): read Retry-After, wait, retry\n  ↓\nAPI server processes request, returns response (status, body)\n  ↓\n(*Request).Into(obj) [rest/request.go:635]\n  1. Deserialize body into obj using NegotiatedSerializer\n  2. Check status code: 2xx = success, non-2xx = structured error\n  3. Return error.StatusError if non-2xx\n  ↓\nuser code: pod is populated or error is returned\n```\n\n**Evidence:** `rest/client.go` (RESTClient.Get, etc.), `rest/request.go` (Do, Into), `rest/transport.go` (buildTransport)\n\n### 3.3 Watched Object Updates via Informer\n\n```\nuser code: factory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, 10*time.Minute)\n           podInformer := factory.Core().V1().Pods()\n           podInformer.Informer().AddEventHandler(handler)\n           factory.Start(stopCh)\n           ↓\nSharedInformerFactory.Start() [informers/factory.go:149]\n  → Spawns goroutines for each informer\n  ↓\nPodInformer.Informer().Run() [informers/core/v1/pod.go]\n  → Creates sharedIndexInformer instance\n  ↓\nsharedIndexInformer.Run(stopCh) [tools/cache/shared_informer.go:325]\n  1. Starts Reflector in a dedicated goroutine\n  2. Starts controller (Pop DeltaFIFO, update cache)\n  ↓\nReflector.ListAndWatch() [tools/cache/reflector.go:350]\n  1. LIST: clientset.CoreV1().Pods().List(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{Limit: 500})\n     → GET /api/v1/pods?limit=500&continue=<token> (paginated)\n     → Populates cache with all pods\n     → Gets resourceVersion \"12345\" from list metadata\n  2. WATCH: clientset.CoreV1().Pods().Watch(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{ResourceVersion: \"12345\"})\n     → GET /api/v1/pods?watch=true&resourceVersion=12345\n     → Streams watch.Event objects (ADDED, MODIFIED, DELETED, BOOKMARK)\n     → Reflector.Add/Update/Delete calls → DeltaFIFO.Add/Update/Delete\n  3. On watch error (io.EOF, connection reset):\n     → Backoff, re-LIST with latest resourceVersion\n  4. Periodically consumes bookmarks to keep resourceVersion fresh\n  ↓\nDeltaFIFO receives deltas from Reflector\n  → Accumulates as Deltas[object, \"MODIFIED\", object, \"MODIFIED\", ...]\n  ↓\nController.processLoop() [tools/cache/controller.go:185]\n  Pops from DeltaFIFO repeatedly:\n  1. deltasInterface := queue.Pop()  // Deltas for one object\n  2. For each delta in Deltas:\n     → Update Indexer cache\n     → Invoke registered event handlers (AddFunc, UpdateFunc, DeleteFunc)\n  3. Event handler receives object:\n     → DOES NOT call user code directly (would block watch stream)\n     → Calls workQueue.Add(\"namespace/name\")  ← adds work item\n  ↓\nUser's controller worker [user code loop]:\n  1. Get next item from workQueue\n  2. Fetch object from cache via Lister\n  3. Reconcile (call API, update status, etc.)\n  4. On success: workQueue.Done(item)\n  5. On transient error: workQueue.AddRateLimited(item)  ← backoff retry\n  ↓\nLoop continues until stopCh is closed\n```\n\n**Evidence:** `informers/factory.go:149-166` (Start), `tools/cache/shared_informer.go:325-345` (Run), `tools/cache/reflector.go:350-450` (ListAndWatch), `tools/cache/controller.go:185-210` (processLoop)\n\n### 3.4 Dynamic Client with Discovery\n\n```\nuser code: gvr := schema.GroupVersionResource{Group: \"example.com\", Version: \"v1\", Resource: \"foos\"}\n           obj, err := dynClient.Resource(gvr).Namespace(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-foo\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n  ↓\nDynamicClient.Resource(gvr) [dynamic/simple.go:103]\n  → Returns ResourceInterface for this GVR\n  ↓\nResourceInterface.Namespace(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-foo\", metav1.GetOptions{}) [dynamic/simple.go:140]\n  1. Check discovery: is \"foos\" namespaced?\n     → Call discoveryClient.ServerResourcesForGroupVersion(\"example.com/v1\")\n     → Returns list of resources + their properties (namespaced: true/false)\n  2. Build REST URL based on namespace scope\n  3. Call underlying rest.Client (same as typed client)\n  ↓\nrest.Client performs GET request (identical to typed flow)\n  ↓\nResponse deserialized into *unstructured.Unstructured (map-based representation)\n```\n\n**Evidence:** `dynamic/simple.go:103-160` (Resource, Namespace), `dynamic/simple.go:140` (Get)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### 4.1.1 Watch Stream Goes Stale (\"too old resourceVersion\")\n\n**Symptom:**\n```\nHTTP 410 Gone: the object has been deleted because the watch stream fell too far behind\n```\n\n**Root Cause:**\n- Reflector was paused (e.g., due to slow event handler goroutine)\n- Watch stream disconnected; reconnect attempted with stale resourceVersion\n- API server's watch cache (default ~5min) has already discarded that version\n\n**Mitigation:**\n1. **Bookmarks** (KEP-1904): API server sends BOOKMARK events with fresh resourceVersion\n   - Reflector consumes bookmarks, advancing restart point without full re-list\n   - Reduces cost of recovery when watch is merely slow, not stale\n2. **Automatic re-list**: Reflector detects 410 error, performs full LIST, resumes WATCH\n3. **User-controlled resyncPeriod**: Periodic re-list (e.g., every 10 minutes) ensures catch-up even if watch somehow falls behind\n\n**Evidence:** `tools/cache/reflector.go:220-240` (isExpiredError, LIST recovery)\n\n#### 4.1.2 API Server Becomes Unreachable\n\n**Symptom:**\n- All requests fail with connection timeouts\n- Informer watches stuck (cannot reconnect)\n\n**Mitigation:**\n1. **Client-side rate limiting**: RESTClient returns errors immediately when API is unreachable; exponential backoff in controller's retry loop prevents thundering herd\n2. **Discovery caching**: Tools like kubectl can still work if they cached discovery data (e.g., in `~/.kube/cache/discovery`)\n3. **Controller's work queue**: Decouples watch (which is stuck) from reconciliation logic; items remain queued during outage, retried after recovery\n\n**Limitation:** In-process cache becomes stale; no updates for duration of outage. Controllers must tolerate eventual consistency.\n\n#### 4.1.3 Concurrent Modification Conflicts\n\n**Scenario:**\nTwo controllers both call `Update()` on the same object without coordination.\n\n**Symptom:**\n```\nHTTP 409 Conflict: the object has been modified; refresh and retry\n```\n\n**Mitigation:**\n1. **Traditional approach**: Use Server-Side Apply instead of Update (allows shared ownership)\n2. **Leader election**: Only one controller manages the object at a time\n3. **Optimistic locking**: Check `metadata.resourceVersion` before updating; if mismatch, retry\n\n**Evidence:** `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go` (Lease-based lock), `applyconfigurations/` (server-side apply pattern)\n\n#### 4.1.4 Memory Pressure from Large Cache\n\n**Scenario:**\nController watching millions of objects; Indexer cache consumes significant memory.\n\n**Symptom:**\n- OOMKilled pod (if deployed in Kubernetes)\n- Slow GC pauses due to large heap\n\n**Mitigation:**\n1. **Selective watching**: Only add event handler for objects in specific namespace or label selector\n   - Reflector respects `FieldSelector` and `LabelSelector` in ListOptions\n   - API server returns fewer objects; cache is smaller\n2. **Resync period tuning**: Reduce resyncPeriod if periodic reprocessing is expensive\n3. **Custom indexing**: Only index on critical fields (namespace, owner references); avoid indexing large label maps\n\n**Design Tradeoff:** In-process caching trades memory for latency (cache lookups are O(1) vs. API calls which are O(100ms+))\n\n#### 4.1.5 Event Handler Panic\n\n**Scenario:**\nUser's event handler panics.\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Goroutine crashes\n- Event stream stops for that informer\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Informers recover panics internally; panics are logged but don't crash the watch\n- Work items are not added if handler panics, so reconciliation doesn't happen\n- Solution: **Wrap your handler in defer + recover** if you need to ensure other handlers run\n\n**Evidence:** `tools/cache/shared_informer.go:490-510` (processorListener handles panics)\n\n### 4.2 Limits and Constraints\n\n#### 4.2.1 Rate Limiting\n\n**Client-Side (rest.Config):**\n- Default QPS: 5, Burst: 10\n- Enforced per RESTClient instance via token bucket\n- Does NOT enforce cluster-wide limits\n- Can be disabled by setting QPS < 0 and RateLimiter = nil\n\n**Interaction with Server-Side Limits:**\n- API Priority and Fairness (APF): Server has separate rate limiting by priority level, flow schema\n- Client QPS + Burst settings coordinate with server's APF; they are two independent rate limits\n\n**Lesson:** Setting client QPS=1000 does not mean requests arrive at 1000/sec; APF may throttle them further\n\n#### 4.2.2 Watch Stream Timeouts\n\n**Default minWatchTimeout:** 5 minutes (randomized to [5m, 10m) to spread load)\n\n**Implication:**\n- Watch streams are deliberately short-lived to allow graceful API server scaling (e.g., restarting kube-apiserver)\n- Controllers must be prepared for frequent watch reconnects\n- Exponential backoff prevents reconnect thundering\n\n**Tuning:** `Config.MinWatchTimeout` can be increased for slow clients, but values < 5min are ignored (enforced server-side)\n\n#### 4.2.3 List Pagination\n\n**Default page size:** 500 (controlled by API server)\n\n**Impact:**\n- Large LIST operations are chunked; client must handle continue tokens\n- `Reflector.ListAndWatch()` internally handles pagination; users typically don't see it\n- Exception: `DynamicClient.List()` with large result sets may require manual pagination\n\n**Code Location:** `tools/cache/listwatch.go:93` (NewListWatchFromClient handles pagination)\n\n#### 4.2.4 Cache Resync Skew\n\n**Scenario:**\nMultiple SharedInformerFactories with different resyncPeriods create thundering herd during resync windows.\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Each Reflector adds random jitter to resync interval (±10%)\n- Stagger initial resync times to avoid all informers re-listing simultaneously\n\n**Evidence:** `tools/cache/reflector.go:162-170` (resyncPeriod + jitter)\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### 4.3.1 Eventual Consistency vs. Strong Consistency\n\n**client-go Design:** Eventual consistency\n\n- Objects in the cache may lag API server state by seconds (watch propagation time) or minutes (if watch stream is stale)\n- Reads from cache are fast (O(1)) but potentially stale\n- Writes go through API server (always authoritative)\n\n**Implication:**\n- Controllers **cannot assume** that a recently-updated object is visible in the cache\n- Must add defensive checks: \"object I just created is not in cache? Retry.\"\n- Acceptable for most Kubernetes controllers (reconciliation loops are idempotent)\n\n#### 4.3.2 Single-Writer (Leader Election) vs. Multi-Writer (Server-Side Apply)\n\n| Pattern | Use Case | Tradeoff |\n|---------|----------|----------|\n| Leader Election (`tools/leaderelection/`) | Only one controller active at a time | Simple, but single point of failure during leadership transfer |\n| Server-Side Apply (`applyconfigurations/`) | Multiple controllers manage different fields | Requires schema awareness of field ownership, more complex coordination |\n\n**Evidence:**\n- Leader election: `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`\n- Server-Side Apply: `applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment_applyconfiguration.go` (generated)\n\n#### 4.3.3 Typed Client (compile-time) vs. Dynamic Client (runtime)\n\n| Model | Use Case | Tradeoff |\n|-------|----------|----------|\n| **Typed** (`kubernetes.Clientset`) | Built-in Kubernetes APIs | Requires code generation for new types; type-safe |\n| **Dynamic** (`dynamic.DynamicClient`) | CRDs, extensible APIs | No code generation needed; discover at runtime; no type safety |\n\n**Performance Implication:**\n- Typed: No discovery overhead (types known at compile time)\n- Dynamic: Must call discovery on first access to determine namespace scope; future accesses cached\n\n#### 4.3.4 Caching Model: DeltaFIFO vs. Simple Store\n\n**DeltaFIFO:**\n- Accumulates per-object history (Deltas)\n- Allows consumers to see the full sequence of changes (Added → Modified → Modified → Deleted)\n- Higher memory overhead (stores all deltas until popped)\n\n**Simple Store (List-Watch without DeltaFIFO):**\n- Stores only current state\n- Lower memory, but loses intermediate events\n\n**Design Decision:** client-go uses DeltaFIFO by default because controllers often need to reconcile state correctly after a burst of rapid changes. Storing intermediate deltas allows controllers to avoid missing state.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Transport Middleware\n\n**Hook:** `rest.Config.WrapTransport`\n\n```go\nconfig.WrapTransport = func(rt http.RoundTripper) http.RoundTripper {\n  return &customRoundTripper{next: rt}\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Custom request/response logging\n- Metrics collection (latency, error rates per endpoint)\n- Request/response mutation (e.g., strip sensitive headers before logging)\n- Protocol upgrades (e.g., ALPN for HTTP/2)\n\n**Evidence:** `rest/config.go:800-820` (buildTransport uses WrapTransport)\n\n### 5.2 Content Negotiation and Serialization\n\n**Hook:** `rest.Config.ContentConfig`\n\n```go\nconfig.ContentConfig.ContentType = \"application/json\"  // default\nconfig.ContentConfig.AcceptContentTypes = \"application/json;q=0.9,application/cbor;q=1\"  // prefer CBOR, fallback JSON\nconfig.NegotiatedSerializer = custom.Serializer{}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Switch to Protobuf for bandwidth optimization (default is JSON)\n- Use CBOR for even smaller payload sizes (v1.28+)\n- Implement custom serialization for domain-specific types\n\n**Evidence:** `rest/client.go:79-93` (ClientContentConfig), `dynamic/simple.go:42-59` (ConfigFor handles CBOR feature gates)\n\n### 5.3 Custom Rate Limiters\n\n**Hook:** `rest.Config.RateLimiter`\n\n```go\nconfig.RateLimiter = workqueue.NewMaxOfRateLimiter(\n  workqueue.NewItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter(5*time.Millisecond, 1000*time.Second),\n  &workqueue.BucketRateLimiter{Limiter: rate.NewLimiter(rate.Limit(100), 1)},\n)\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Exponential backoff for transient errors\n- Fixed-rate bucket limiter for sustained load\n- Combination of multiple limiters (e.g., exponential backoff + max rate)\n\n**Evidence:** `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go` (various rate limiter implementations)\n\n### 5.4 Event Handlers\n\n**Hook:** `Informer.AddEventHandler` or `Informer.AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod`\n\n```go\ninformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n  AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n    key, _ := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n    workQueue.Add(key)\n  },\n  UpdateFunc: func(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n    // Compare oldObj and newObj, maybe add to queue\n  },\n  DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n    key, _ := cache.DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n    workQueue.Add(key)\n  },\n})\n```\n\n**Constraints:**\n- Must complete quickly (blocks watch event processing if slow)\n- Must not call external APIs or perform I/O\n- Should not panic (though recoverable)\n- Multiple handlers execute sequentially; order is FIFO registration order\n\n**Evidence:** `tools/cache/shared_informer.go:440-460` (AddEventHandler registration), `tools/cache/processor_listener.go` (handler invocation)\n\n### 5.5 Custom Indexing\n\n**Hook:** `Indexer.AddIndexers` (on cache construction)\n\n```go\nindexers := cache.Indexers{\n  \"ownerReference\": func(obj interface{}) ([]string, error) {\n    pod := obj.(*corev1.Pod)\n    var keys []string\n    for _, ref := range pod.ObjectMeta.OwnerReferences {\n      keys = append(keys, fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", ref.Kind, ref.Name))\n    }\n    return keys, nil\n  },\n}\nindexer := cache.NewIndexer(cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Index by owner references for fast child lookups\n- Index by labels or annotations for custom queries\n- Index by external identifiers (e.g., cloud resource IDs)\n\n**Performance Implication:**\n- Index is maintained during `Add`, `Update`, `Delete` operations\n- Queries via `ByIndex()` are O(1) + O(n filtered results)\n\n**Evidence:** `tools/cache/index.go` (Indexer interface and methods), `informers/core/v1/pod.go` (example: namespace indexing)\n\n### 5.6 Custom Work Queue\n\n**Hook:** `util/workqueue` provides multiple queue implementations\n\n```go\n// Default FIFO\nq := workqueue.New()\n\n// With exponential backoff\nq := workqueue.NewRateLimitingQueue(workqueue.DefaultControllerRateLimiter())\n\n// With priority\nq := workqueue.NewPriorityQueue(workqueue.DefaultQueueConfig())\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Priority queues (process high-priority items first)\n- Delayed queues (process items at specific times)\n- Custom backoff strategies (e.g., jittered exponential backoff)\n\n**Evidence:** `util/workqueue/queue.go`, `util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go`, `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go`\n\n### 5.7 Custom Leader Election\n\n**Hook:** `tools/leaderelection.LeaderElectionConfig`\n\n```go\nleConfig := leaderelection.LeaderElectionConfig{\n  Lock: &resourcelock.LeaseLock{\n    LeaseMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{\n      Name:      \"my-controller-lock\",\n      Namespace: \"default\",\n    },\n    Client: coordClient,\n    LockConfig: resourcelock.ResourceLockConfig{\n      Identity: hostname,\n    },\n  },\n  LeaseDuration: 15 * time.Second,\n  RenewDeadline: 10 * time.Second,\n  RetryPeriod:   5 * time.Second,\n  Callbacks: leaderelection.LeaderCallbacks{\n    OnNewLeader: func(identity string) {\n      log.Infof(\"New leader: %s\", identity)\n    },\n    OnStoppedLeading: func() {\n      log.Info(\"Lost leadership\")\n    },\n  },\n}\nelector := leaderelection.NewLeaderElector(leConfig)\nelector.Run(ctx)\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Adjust lease duration based on cluster size (larger clusters need longer durations)\n- Custom lock implementations (ConfigMap instead of Lease)\n- Custom leader callbacks (emit metrics, graceful shutdown on leadership loss)\n\n**Evidence:** `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go:100-200` (Config, NewLeaderElector)\n\n### 5.8 Custom Watch Error Handling\n\n**Hook:** `Config.WatchErrorHandler` (deprecated) or `Config.WatchErrorHandlerWithContext`\n\n```go\nconfig := &rest.Config{...}\nconfig.WatchErrorHandlerWithContext = func(ctx context.Context, r *cache.Reflector, err error) {\n  switch {\n  case apierrors.IsExpiredError(err):\n    // Handle stale watch error\n    metrics.WatchStaleCount.Inc()\n  default:\n    // Custom error handling\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Custom metrics for watch errors\n- Alerting on specific error patterns\n- Custom logging formats\n\n**Evidence:** `tools/cache/reflector.go:191-210` (DefaultWatchErrorHandler), `tools/cache/controller.go:125-135` (Config.WatchErrorHandler)\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Memory\n\n**Typical Consumption:**\n- ~1 KB per small object (Pod) in cache\n- 100,000 Pods ≈ 100 MB cache\n- Add 20-30% overhead for indices and synchronization primitives\n\n**Optimization:**\n- Reduce watch scope (namespace selectors, label selectors)\n- Tune resyncPeriod (less frequent = smaller periodic LIST overhead)\n- Custom indexing on essential fields only\n\n**Monitoring:**\n```\ngo_memstats_heap_alloc_bytes  # total heap memory\ninformer_cache_populate_duration_seconds  # LIST/WATCH latency\n```\n\n#### Latency\n\n**Object Update Latency (from API server to cache):**\n- Watch propagation: typically 10-100 ms\n- Plus event handler delay + work queue processing\n- Total: 100-500 ms typical for simple controllers\n\n**Optimization:**\n- Minimize event handler work (add to queue only)\n- Use rate limiting only for retries, not success path\n- Profile slow handlers with pprof\n\n**Monitoring:**\n```\nworkqueue_adds_total  # new items entering queue\nworkqueue_depth  # queue length (backlog indicator)\nworkqueue_work_duration_seconds  # actual reconciliation time\n```\n\n#### Network\n\n**Bandwidth per controller:**\n- LIST operation: O(number of objects)\n- WATCH: small per event (delta only, not full object)\n- Resync: full LIST again (avoid if possible)\n\n**Optimization:**\n- Use FieldSelector to reduce LIST results (server-side filtering)\n- Reduce resyncPeriod if not needed\n- Use dynamic client sparingly (adds discovery overhead)\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Recovery\n\n#### Graceful Shutdown\n\n```go\nstopCh := make(chan struct{})\nfactory.Start(stopCh)\n\n// On SIGTERM\nsigCh := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(sigCh, syscall.SIGTERM)\n<-sigCh\nclose(stopCh)\n\n// Wait for informers to stop (max 30 sec grace period)\ntime.Sleep(30 * time.Second)\n```\n\n**Key Point:** Closing stopCh does not immediately stop all goroutines; give them time to finish draining work queue before exiting.\n\n#### Crash Recovery\n\n**What happens when controller pod is deleted/restarted:**\n1. All in-memory cache is lost\n2. Lease lock (for leader election) is released (after leaseDuration expires or actively renounced)\n3. New instance restarts with cold cache\n4. Reflector re-LISTs to repopulate\n5. Controller resumes processing work queue items\n\n**Implication:** Reconciliation must be idempotent (applying same desired state twice yields same result).\n\n#### Watch Stream Stale Handling\n\n**Automatic recovery:**\n```\nHTTP 410 error (watch too old)\n→ Reflector backoffs with exponential jitter\n→ Re-LIST with fresh resourceVersion\n→ Resume WATCH\n→ No events lost during re-LIST window (already accumulated in work queue)\n```\n\n**Monitoring:**\n```\nreflector_lists_total  # count of LIST operations (high = frequent staleness recovery)\nreflector_list_duration_seconds  # LIST latency\n```\n\n### 6.3 Observability and Debugging\n\n#### Key Metrics\n\n1. **Reflector health:**\n   - `reflector_lists_total`: Incrementing slowly (healthy) vs. rapidly (watch is stale)\n   - `reflector_list_duration_seconds`: Latency of LIST operations\n   - `reflector_watch_duration_seconds`: Watch stream length (longer = healthier)\n\n2. **Work queue health:**\n   - `workqueue_depth`: Should be low (0-10) in steady state; high = backed up\n   - `workqueue_adds_total`: Event rate\n   - `workqueue_work_duration_seconds`: Reconciliation latency\n   - `workqueue_retries_total`: Failed reconciliations (should be low)\n\n3. **Informer cache health:**\n   - `informer_cache_size`: Number of objects in cache\n   - `informer_cache_populate_duration_seconds`: Time to sync cache on startup\n\n#### Logging\n\n**Enable verbose logging:**\n```go\nklog.SetLogger(klog.NewKlogr())\n// In Kubernetes, --v=4 enables client-go debug logs\n```\n\n**Useful debug logs:**\n```\nV(4) \"Watch closed\" reflector=... type=... err=...  # watch disconnects\nV(5) \"Reflector.Run\" -> \"ListAndWatch\" -> \"WatchHandler\" -> events\nV(6) \"DeltaFIFO\" pop/push operations\n```\n\n#### Debugging Specific Issues\n\n**Informer not syncing:**\n```go\nif !cache.WaitForCacheSync(stopCh, informer.HasSynced) {\n  log.Fatal(\"Timed out waiting for cache sync\")  // Debug: check if LIST is slow\n}\n```\n\n**Hanging event handlers:**\n```\n// Add timeouts to event handlers\nAddEventHandler(\n  cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n      ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 1*time.Second)\n      defer cancel()\n      // process with timeout\n    },\n  },\n)\n```\n\n**Controller stuck in backoff:**\n```\n// Check work queue depth and retry count\nfor {\n  item, shutdown := workQueue.Get()\n  if shutdown { break }\n  // If retry count high, likely hitting API errors\n  retryCount := cache.GetExponentialBackoffCount(item)\n  log.Infof(\"Reconciling %v, retry %d\", item, retryCount)\n}\n```\n\n### 6.4 Scaling Considerations\n\n#### Scaling to Many Objects\n\n**Problem:** Single controller watching 100k+ Pods hits memory/CPU limits.\n\n**Solutions:**\n1. **Shard by namespace:** Deploy separate controller per namespace\n2. **Shard by label selector:** Each controller watches subset of objects\n3. **Use dynamic client:** Discover and query only needed types (avoid loading all API group versions)\n\n**Code:**\n```go\n// Namespace-specific informer\nfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions(\n  clientset,\n  10*time.Minute,\n  informers.WithNamespace(\"default\"),  // Only watch this namespace\n)\n```\n\n#### Scaling to Many Controllers\n\n**Problem:** 10+ controllers all watching same Pods, each opens separate LIST/WATCH connection.\n\n**Solution:** Use shared informers\n```go\n// Share single informer across controllers\nfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, 10*time.Minute)\npodInformer := factory.Core().V1().Pods()\npodInformer.Informer().AddEventHandler(controller1Handler)\npodInformer.Informer().AddEventHandler(controller2Handler)\nfactory.Start(stopCh)\n```\n\n**Benefit:** Single LIST/WATCH for multiple controllers; events fan out to all handlers.\n\n#### API Server Burst Protection\n\n**Scenario:** Cluster-wide event (e.g., node restart) causes many Pods to change; all controllers stampede.\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- `Config.QPS` and `Config.Burst` limit per-client rate\n- API Priority and Fairness (APF) on server limits per controller priority level\n- Work queue rate limiting adds exponential backoff per item (not per API call)\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n### Core Request/Response Layer\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `rest/config.go` | rest.Config structure; configuration loading |\n| `rest/client.go` | RESTClient; ResourceInterface for untyped resources |\n| `dynamic/scheme.go` | Unstructured object scheme |\n\n### Discovery\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `discovery/discovery_client.go` | `discovery/aggregated_discovery.go` | Newer aggregated discovery format (APIGroupDiscoveryList) |\n| `discovery/helper.go` | Helper functions for querying discovery |\n\n### Controller Infrastructure\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `tools/cache/reflector.go` | Reflector: LIST and WATCH synchronization |\n| `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` | DeltaFIFO: per-object change for cache access |\n| `tools/cache/listwatch.go` | ListerWatcher: LIST and WATCH client |\n| `informers/factory.go` | SharedInformerFactory: factory for all typed informers |\n| `informers/{core,apps,...}/v{1,1beta1,...}/` | Generated typed informers per API group |\n| `listers/{core,apps,...}/v{1,1beta1,...}/` | Generated typed listers per API group |\n\n### Work Queue and Coordination\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `util/workqueue/queue.go` | FIFO queue interface and implementation |\n| `util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go` | DelayingQueue for scheduled re-queuing |\n| `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go` | RateLimitingQueue with configurable backoff |\n| `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go` | Built-in rate limiters (exponential backoff, max retries) |\n| `util/workqueue/metrics.go` | Prometheus metrics for queue depth, latency |\n| `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go` | LeaderElector using Lease locks |\n| `tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/` | Lock implementations (Lease, ConfigMap) |\n\n### Server-Side Apply\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `applyconfigurations/{core,apps,...}/v{1,1beta1,...}/` | Generated type-safe builders for each API type |\n| `util/apply/apply.go` | Helper functions for constructing apply patches |\n\n### Utilities\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `util/flowcontrol/` | Token bucket rate limiting |\n| `util/certificate/` | Client certificate management for mTLS |\n| `util/cert/` | TLS certificate parsing and validation |\n| `util/retry/` | Retry logic primitives |\n| `tools/clientcmd/` | kubeconfig loading and context merging |\n| `tools/pager/` | LIST pagination helpers |\n|
